There are differences between both issues of course, but to attack an AG for enforcing a well intentioned law are doing so because of only the negative results, and not even acknowledging any positives that came via alternatives such as diversionary programs.
Families who get dinged for truancy law violations are often suffering and need social services they may not know they have access to, similarly to those kids with the curfew violations. Enforcing those laws is a way to ultimately guide them towards resources that may help.
I met with people who did arrest sweeps as part of the planning process, scoped locations, made educational materials, etc. I was the lead "assistant" on this. We also watched vids about other cities' curfew laws and just shook our heads at how blatant their issues were.
The point was- 1. Let's keep kids out of the system for dumb things like curfew violations &amp; truancy. 2. Let's actually give them help. 3. Let's show how useful diversionary things like curbside/stationhouse adjustments are. 4 Let's show that the chaplaincy programs work.
A coalition, made up of police, the county ag, basically every relevant social service agency within the county, &amp; the group I was with did a special curfew sweep with the newer police chaplaincy programs as a result of finding this.
1 of my old jobs involved me organizing &amp; mapping juvenile arrest records. We found that in the 3 main cities/towns I looked at, curfew violations were abnormally high in terms of arrest rates compared to crimes that were actually serious.
There's gonna be so many bs attacks on Kamala about actually enforcing truancy laws when people don't comprehend that prosecutors &amp; law enforcement also don't like them, but many use them to steer people towards social services &amp; programs that actually help the kids &amp; families.
